<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=CENTER>
	-16-
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX; PADDING-TOP:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage17"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<U>
	Construction Activity
</U>
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	The Company is directly impacted by the level of single family and multi-family residential housing starts and, to a lesser extent, commercial construction starts. The construction industry can be cyclical, shifting upwards and downwards depending on a variety of factors. &nbsp;After a few years of significant building, the United States construction industry appeared to hit a peak in 2006. &nbsp;Low interest rates and easy availability of credit, contributed to a high level of construction activity. However, following that period, the industry experienced a significant deterioration in demand for residential, commercial and institutional construction. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	Some of the factors that influenced the decline include:
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:12PT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&#183;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	the crisis in the financial markets reduced the availability of financing for new construction, especially large projects
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:12PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&#183;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	foreclosures had increased the inventory of available residential housing, thereby decreasing the demand for new construction, and
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:12PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&#183;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	consumer demand and confidence declined as a result of reduced economic activity and increased unemployment.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; CLEAR:LEFT">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:-1.6PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During 2014 and 2015, the construction activity appeared to reflect a recovery, and has shown upward mobility. Projections published by the National Association of Home Builders predicts housing starts will continue to increase during 2016. However, any significant decrease in residential construction activity may materially adversely affect the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s financial condition.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:46.4PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<U>
	Technological Changes
</U>
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	Although the HVAC industry has historically been impacted by technology changes in a relatively incremental manner, it cannot be discounted that radical changes might impact the use of natural gas, which could materially adversely affect the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s results of operations and/or financial position in the future, but at this time it does not appear that there are any known technologies that could negatively impact the market materially.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<U>
	Weather Conditions
</U>
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	The Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s flagship TracPipe
<SUP>
	&#174;
</SUP>
	and CounterStrike
<SUP>
	&#174;
</SUP>
	products are used in residential and commercial heating applications. As such, the demand for its products is impacted by weather as it affects the level of construction. Furthermore, severe climatic changes, such as those suggested by the
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	global climate change
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	phenomenon, could over time adversely affect the demand for fossil fuel heating products and adversely affect the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s results of operations and financial position.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<U>
	Purchasing Practices
</U>
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	It has been the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s policy in recent years to aggregate purchase volumes for high value commodities with fewer vendors to achieve maximum volume related cost reductions while maintaining quality and service. This policy has been effective in reducing costs, but has introduced additional risk which could potentially result in short-term supply disruptions or cost increases from time to time in the future if one of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s key vendors experiences any catastrophic event, such as bankruptcy.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<U>
	Legal Costs
</U>
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	The Company is subject to lawsuits mostly relating to claims of product liability. &nbsp;The Company has in place insurance policies to cover the defense of most of these cases, and any amounts payable with respect thereto, which are typically subject to deductibles or self-insured retention amounts that vary depending on the policy year. &nbsp;In 2013, the Company won two cases at two separate trials.&#160; In both cases, the jury unanimously found that the Company was not negligent in designing its TracPipe&#174; product, and that the TracPipe&#174; product was not defective or unreasonably dangerous.&#160; In 2014, the Company won an appeal at the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania from a portion of an adverse jury verdict from an earlier trial. &nbsp;As a result of that decision, the Pennsylvania Supreme Court rewrote the law in Pennsylvania regarding product liability.&#160; That case has been returned to the trial court for further hearings.&#160; Finally, the Company was successful in obtaining the dismissal of two attempted class action cases that were filed against the Company.&#160; In both cases the lead plaintiffs did not allege any actual harm had occurred, and the courts dismissed both those actions. &nbsp;However, continued litigation and the defense costs associated therewith, in addition to any other payments made, could affect the Company's results of operations, perhaps materially, and could potentially affect the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s ability to obtain insurance through mainstream markets at an affordable price.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=CENTER>
	-17-
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX; PADDING-TOP:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage18"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<U>
	Supply Disruptions and Commodity Risks
</U>
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	The Company uses a variety of materials in the manufacture of its products, including stainless steel for its CSST, polyethylene which is used as a jacket for the CSST, as well as its previously documented electrical dispersion properties, and brass for its fittings. In connection with the purchase of commodities, principally stainless steel for manufacturing requirements, the Company occasionally enters into one-year purchase commitments which include a designated fixed price or range of prices. &nbsp;These agreements sometimes require the Company to accept delivery of the commodity in the quantities committed, at the agreed upon prices. &nbsp;Transactions required for these commodities in excess of the one year commitments are conducted at current market prices at the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s discretion. &nbsp;Currently, the Company does not have any fixed purchase commitment contracts, but may enter into such transactions in the future. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Management believes at present that it has adequate sources of supply for its raw materials and components (subject to the risks described above under Purchasing Practices) and has historically not had significant difficulty in obtaining the raw materials, component parts or finished goods from its suppliers. The Company is not dependent for any commodity on a single supplier, the loss of which would have a material adverse effect on its business.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<U>
	Interest Rate Sensitivity
</U>
	- The Company currently has access to a $15,000,000 unsecured line of credit (LOC) with Santander Bank, formerly Sovereign Bank, NA (Sovereign), and as of December 31, 2015, has no outstanding amounts due on the line. &nbsp;When the Company borrows against the LOC, all amounts must be paid back with interest, using an interest rate range of LIBOR plus 1.00% to LIBOR plus 1.35% or the Prime rate up to Prime plus 0.10%, depending upon the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s then existing financial ratios. &nbsp;The Company may elect to use either the LIBOR or PRIME rates. &nbsp;As of December 31, 2015, the actual rate to borrow was at approximately 1.61%. &nbsp;Interest rates are also significant to the Company as a participant in the residential construction industry, since interest rates can be a determinant factor on whether or not borrowing funds for building will be affordable to our customers. &nbsp;(See Construction Activity, above). Currently, interest rates are currently reasonably low, but any dramatic change to interest rates could have a detrimental effect on the business.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<U>
	Retention of Qualified Personnel
</U>
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8211;
</FONT>
	The Company does not operate with multiple levels of management. It is relatively
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	flat
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	organizationally, which does subject the Company to the risks associated with the loss of critical managers. From time to time, there may be a shortage of skilled labor, which may make it more difficult and expensive for the Company to attract and retain qualified employees. The Company is dependent upon the relatively unique talents and managerial skills of a small number of key executives. &nbsp;The Company utilizes a phantom stock program as a retention tool targeted at such key executives and employees, as outlined in Note 12 of the consolidated financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	CRITICAL ACCOUNTING POLICIES AND USE OF ESTIMATES
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Financial Reporting Release No. 60, released by the Securities and Exchange Commission, requires all companies to include a discussion of critical accounting policies or methods used in the preparation of financial statements. Note 2 of the Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements includes a summary of the significant accounting policies and methods used in the preparation of our Consolidated Financial Statements. The following is a brief discussion of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s more significant accounting policies.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP) requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and the disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the dates of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting periods. The most significant estimates and assumptions relate to revenue recognition, accounts receivable allowances, inventory valuations, goodwill valuation, product liability costs, phantom stock and accounting for income taxes. &nbsp;Actual amounts could differ significantly from these estimates.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=CENTER>
	-18-
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX; PADDING-TOP:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage19"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
	Our critical accounting policies and significant estimates and assumptions are described in more detail as follows:
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Revenue Recognition
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s revenue recognition activities relate almost entirely to the manufacture and sale of flexible metal hose and pipe. Under GAAP, revenues are considered to have been earned when the Company has substantially accomplished what it must do to be entitled to the benefits represented by the revenues. &nbsp;The following criteria represent preconditions to the recognition of revenue:
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:26.867PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:12PT; FLOAT:LEFT">
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#61623;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:26.867PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	Persuasive evidence of an arrangement for the sale of product or services must exist.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:26.867PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:12PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#61623;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:26.867PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	Delivery has occurred or services rendered.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:26.867PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:12PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#61623;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:26.867PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	The sales price to the customer is fixed or determinable.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:26.867PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:12PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#61623;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:26.867PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	Collection is reasonably assured.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; CLEAR:LEFT">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	The Company recognizes revenue upon shipment in accordance with the above principles.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Gross sales are reduced for all consideration paid to customers for which no identifiable benefit is received by the Company. This includes promotional incentives, which includes various programs including year-end rebates, and payment term discounts. The amounts of certain incentives are known with reasonable certainty at the time of sale, while others are projected based upon the most reliable information available at the reporting date. &nbsp;Commissions are accounted for as a selling expense.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Accounts Receivable and Provision for Doubtful Accounts
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Accounts receivable are reduced by an allowance for amounts that may become uncollectible in the future. The estimated allowance for uncollectible amounts is based primarily on specific analysis of accounts in the receivable portfolio and historical write-off experience. While management believes the allowance to be adequate, if the financial condition of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s customers were to deteriorate, resulting in their inability to make payments, additional allowances may be required.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Inventories
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Inventories are valued at the lower of cost or market. &nbsp;The cost of inventories is determined by the first-in, first-out (FIFO) method. &nbsp;The Company generally considers inventory quantities beyond two years of non-usage, measured on a historical usage basis, to be excess inventory and reduces the gross carrying value of inventory accordingly.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Goodwill
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In accordance with Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) ASC Topic 350, Intangibles
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8211;
</FONT>
	Goodwill and Other, the Company performed an annual impairment test in accordance with this guidance as of December 31, 2015 and also at December 31, 2014. &nbsp;These analyses did not indicate any impairment of goodwill at the end of either period.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Stock Based Compensation Plans
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In 2006, the Company adopted a Phantom Stock Plan (the
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	Plan
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	), which allows the Company to grant phantom stock units (Units) to certain key employees, officers or directors. &nbsp;The Units each represent a contractual right to payment of compensation in the future based upon the market value of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s common stock. &nbsp;The Units follow a vesting schedule of three years from the grant date, and are then paid upon maturity. &nbsp;In accordance with FASB ASC Topic 718, Stock Compensation, the Company uses the Black-Scholes option pricing model as its method for determining the fair value of the Units. &nbsp;Further details of the Plan are provided in Note 12.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=CENTER>
	-19-
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">

<HR STYLE="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX; PADDING-TOP:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage20"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<B>
<U>
	Product Liability Reserves
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Product liability reserves represent the estimated unpaid amounts under the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s insurance policies with respect to existing claims. &nbsp;The Company uses the most current available data to estimate claims. &nbsp;As explained more fully under Note 11, Commitments and Contingencies, for various product liability claims covered under the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s general liability insurance policies, the Company must pay certain defense and settlement costs within its deductible or self-insured retention limits, ranging primarily from $25,000 to $250,000 per claim, depending on the terms of the policy in the applicable policy year, up to an aggregate amount. &nbsp;The Company is vigorously defending against all known claims.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Fair Value of Financial and Nonfinancial Instruments
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company measures financial instruments in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 820, Fair Value Measurements and Disclosures. &nbsp;The accounting standard defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair value under GAAP, and enhances disclosures about fair value measurements.&#160;&#160;Fair value is defined as the exchange price that would be received for an asset or paid to transfer a liability (an exit price) in the principal or most advantageous market for the asset or liability in an orderly transaction between market participants on the measurement date.&#160;&#160;Valuation techniques used to measure fair value must maximize the use of observable inputs and minimize the use of unobservable inputs. &nbsp;The standard creates a fair value hierarchy which prioritizes the inputs to valuation techniques used to measure fair value into three broad levels as follows: Level 1 inputs are quoted prices (unadjusted) in active markets for identical assets or liabilities; Level 2 inputs are inputs other than quoted prices included within Level 1 that are observable for the asset or liability, either directly or indirectly; and Level 3 inputs are unobservable inputs that reflect the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s own assumptions about the assumptions market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability. The Company relies on its actively traded share value
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8211;
</FONT>
	a level 1 input
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8211;
</FONT>
	in determining the fair value of the reporting unit in its annual impairment test as described in the FASB ASC Topic 350, Intangibles - Goodwill and Other.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; CLEAR:LEFT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Earnings per Common Share
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Basic earnings per share have been computed using the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding. For the periods presented, there are no dilutive securities. &nbsp;Consequently, basic and dilutive earnings per share are the same.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Currency Translation
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Assets and liabilities denominated in foreign currencies are translated into U.S. dollars at exchange rates prevailing on the balance sheet dates. The Statements of Operations are translated into U.S. dollars at average exchange rates for the period. Adjustments resulting from the translation of financial statements are excluded from the determination of income and are accumulated in a separate component of shareholders
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	equity. Exchange gains and losses resulting from foreign currency transactions are included in the Statements of Operations (other income (expense)) in the period in which they occur.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Income Taxes
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company accounts for tax liabilities in accordance with ASC Topic 740, Income Taxes. Under this method the Company recorded tax expense, related deferred taxes and tax benefits, and uncertainties in tax positions.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax consequences attributable to differences between the financial statement carrying amounts of existing assets and liabilities and their respective tax bases. &nbsp;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the years in which those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. &nbsp;The effect on deferred tax assets and liabilities from a change in tax rates is recognized in income in the period that includes the enactment date. &nbsp;A valuation allowance is provided for deferred tax assets if it is more likely than not that these items will either expire before the Company is able to realize the benefit, or that future deductibility is uncertain. No valuation allowance was deemed necessary at December 31, 2015 or 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Also, in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 740, the Company had a reserve for uncertainties in tax positions of $110,000 at December 31, 2015, and $105,000 at December 31, 2014. These reserves are reviewed each quarter.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">

<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s primary cash needs have been related to working capital items, which the Company has largely funded through cash generated from operations. &nbsp;

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

At December 31, 2014, the Company had cash of $22,585,000.

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s cash provided from operating activities was $13,250,000, compared to $14,840,000 of cash provided during 2014, thus decreasing by $1,590,000 between periods. &nbsp;While no item was particularly significant with regards to creating the reduction in cash, it was recognized that the timing of accounts receivable cash collections, higher inventory purchases, and an increase in amounts paid related to product liability claims in 2015 contributed to the decrease.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	As a general trend, the Company tends to deplete cash early in the year, as significant payments are typically made for accrued promotional incentives, incentive compensation, and taxes. &nbsp;Cash has then historically shown a tendency to be restored and accumulated during the latter portion of the year.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

This was all related to capital expenditures for both periods. &nbsp;As anticipated and disclosed in the 2014 Form 10-K, the Company proceeded with extensive renovations at its Exton, Pennsylvania facilities during 2015, including additional machinery and leasehold improvements, which required a greater outlay of cash than in the previous year.

<A NAME="eolPage22"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<B>
<U>
	RECENT ACCOUNTING PRONOUNCEMENTS
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In May 2014, the FASB issued ASU 2014-09,
<I>
	Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606)
</I>
	, requiring an entity to recognize the amount of revenue to which it expects to be entitled for the transfer of promised goods or services to customers. The updated standard will replace most existing revenue recognition guidance in U.S. GAAP when it becomes effective and permits the use of either a full retrospective or retrospective with cumulative effect transition method. The updated standard becomes effective for the Company in the first quarter of fiscal year 2018. Early adoption is permitted beginning in the first quarter of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s 2017 fiscal year. &nbsp;The Company has not yet selected a transition method and is currently evaluating the effect that the updated standard will have on the consolidated financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In July 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-11,
<I>
	Simplifying the Measurement of Inventory (Topic 330)
</I>
	. &nbsp;Under this ASU, inventory will be measured at the
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	lower of cost and net realizable value
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	and options that currently exist for
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	market value
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	will be eliminated. The ASU defines net realizable value as the
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	estimated selling prices in the ordinary course of business, less reasonably predictable costs of completion, disposal, and transportation.
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	No other changes were made to the current guidance on inventory measurement. ASU 2015-11 is effective for interim and annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016. Early application is permitted and should be applied prospectively. &nbsp;The Company is evaluating the provisions of this statement, including which period to adopt, and has not determined what impact the adoption of ASU 2015-11 will have on the Company's financial position or results of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-02,
<I>
	Leases (Topic 842)
</I>
	. &nbsp;Under this ASU, lessees are required to recognize right-of-use assets and lease liabilities for all leases not considered short-term leases. By definition, a short-term lease is one in which: (a) the lease term is 12 months or less and (b) there is not an option to purchase the underlying asset that the lessee is reasonably certain to exercise. For short-term leases, lessees may elect an accounting policy by class of underlying asset under which right-of-use assets and lease liabilities are not recognized and lease payments are generally recognized as expense over the lease term on a straight-line basis. This change will result in lessees recognizing right-of-use assets and lease liabilities for most leases currently accounted for as operating leases under the legacy lease accounting guidance. &nbsp;ASU 2016-02 is effective for interim and annual periods beginning after December 15, 2018. &nbsp;Early adoption is permitted. The Company is evaluating the provisions of this statement, including which period to adopt, and has not determined what impact the adoption of ASU 2016-02 will have on the Company's financial position or results of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company has off-balance sheet obligations or arrangements at December 31, 2015 that relate to purchase commitments for the following year, and also operating lease obligations, which in total equal $18,891,000. The total amount of these obligations at December 31, 2014 was $22,388,000.

An audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.

<EFX_AUDITORS_OPINION>
<A NAME="FIS_AUDITORS_OPINION_2"></A>
<A NAME="eolPage24"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=CENTER>
<B>
	REPORT OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	To the Board of Directors and Shareholders
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	Omega Flex, Inc.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	We have audited Omega Flex, Inc.'s internal control over financial reporting as of December 31, 2015, based on criteria established in
<I>
	Internal Control
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	Integrated Framework
</I>
	issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission in 2013. Omega Flex Inc.
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s management is responsible for maintaining effective internal control over financial reporting and for its assessment of the effectiveness of internal control over financial reporting included in the accompanying Management
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s Report on Internal Control Over Financial Reporting. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on the company's internal control over financial reporting based on our audit.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether effective internal control over financial reporting was maintained in all material respects. Our audit included obtaining an understanding of internal control over financial reporting, assessing the risk that a material weakness exists, and testing and evaluating the design and operating effectiveness of internal control based on the assessed risk. Our audit also included performing such other procedures as we considered necessary in the circumstances. We believe that our audit provides a reasonable basis for our opinion.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	A company's internal control over financial reporting is a process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. A company's internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that
<I>
	(a)
</I>
	pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions of the assets of the company;
<I>
	(b)
</I>
	provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles, and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizations of management and directors of the company; and
<I>
	(c)
</I>
	provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use, or disposition of the company's assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements. Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In our opinion, Omega Flex, Inc. maintained, in all material respects, effective internal control over financial reporting as of December 31, 2015, based on criteria established in
<I>
	Internal Control
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8212;
</FONT>
	Integrated Framework
</I>
	issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission in 2013.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	We have also audited, in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States), the 2015 consolidated financial statements of Omega Flex, Inc. and our report dated March 4, 2016 expressed an unqualified opinion.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:12PT; MARGIN:0PX">

	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s audited consolidated financial statements for the year ended December 31, 2015 and 2014 have been prepared in accordance with accounting standards set by the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB), and with the instructions of Form 10-K and Article 8 of Regulation S-X. &nbsp;All material inter-company accounts and transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company is a leading manufacturer of flexible metal hose, which is used in a variety of applications to carry gases and liquids within their particular applications. &nbsp;The Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s business is controlled as a single operating segment that consists of the manufacture and sale of flexible metal hose and accessories. These applications include carrying liquefied gases in certain processing applications, fuel gases within residential and commercial buildings and vibration absorbers in high vibration applications. The Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s flexible metal piping is also used to carry other types of gases and fluids in a number of industrial applications where the customer requires the piping to have both a degree of flexibility and/or an ability to carry corrosive compounds or mixtures, or to carry at both very high and very low (cryogenic) temperatures.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company manufactures flexible metal hose at its facilities in Exton, Pennsylvania, in the United States, and in Banbury, Oxfordshire in the United Kingdom, and sells its products through distributors, wholesalers and to original equipment manufacturers (
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	OEMs
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	) throughout North America, and in certain European markets.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
	2. SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Use of Estimates
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP) requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and the disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the dates of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting periods. The most significant estimates and assumptions relate to revenue recognition, accounts receivable allowances, inventory valuations, goodwill valuation, product liability costs, phantom stock and accounting for income taxes. Actual amounts could differ significantly from these estimates.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Revenue Recognition
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s revenue recognition activities relate almost entirely to the manufacture and sale of flexible metal hose and pipe. Under GAAP, revenues are considered to have been earned when the Company has substantially accomplished what it must do to be entitled to the benefits represented by the revenues. The following criteria represent preconditions to the recognition of revenue:
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:11PT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&#183;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:11PT">
	Persuasive evidence of an arrangement for the sale of product or services must exist.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:11PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&#183;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:11PT">
	Delivery has occurred or services rendered.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:11PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&#183;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:11PT">
	The sales price to the customer is fixed or determinable.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-2PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; WIDTH:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:'SYMBOL'; FONT-SIZE:11PT; CLEAR:LEFT; FLOAT:LEFT">
	&#183;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-2PX; FONT-SIZE:11PT">
	Collection is reasonably assured.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; CLEAR:LEFT">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	The Company recognizes revenue upon shipment in accordance with the above principles.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Gross sales are reduced for all consideration paid to customers for which no identifiable benefit is received by the Company. This includes promotional incentives, which includes various programs including year-end rebates, and payment term discounts. The amounts of certain incentives are known with reasonable certainty at the time of sale, while others are projected based upon the most reliable information available at the reporting date. Commissions are accounted for as a selling expense.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX">
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=CENTER>
	-30-
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX; PADDING-TOP:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage31"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<B>
<U>
	Cash Equivalents
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company considers all highly liquid investments with an original maturity of 90 days or less at the time of purchase to be cash equivalents. Cash equivalents include investments in an institutional money market fund, which invests in U.S. Treasury bills, notes and bonds, and/or repurchase agreements, backed by such obligations. &nbsp;Carrying value approximates fair value. Cash and cash equivalents are deposited at various area banks, which at times may exceed federally insured limits. &nbsp;The Company monitors the viability of the banking institutions carrying its assets on a regular basis, and has the ability to transfer cash to various institutions during times of risk. &nbsp;The Company has not experienced any losses related to these cash balances, and believes its credit risk to be minimal.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Accounts Receivable and Provision for Doubtful Accounts
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Accounts receivable are reduced by an allowance for amounts that may become uncollectible in the future. The estimated allowance for uncollectible amounts is based primarily on specific analysis of accounts in the receivable portfolio and historical write-off experience. While management believes the allowance to be adequate, if the financial condition of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s customers were to deteriorate, resulting in their inability to make payments, additional allowances may be required.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The allowance for doubtful accounts reflects our best estimate of probable losses inherent in the accounts receivable balance. &nbsp;The Company determines the allowance based on any known collection issues, historical experience, and other currently available evidence. &nbsp;The reserve for future credits, discounts, and doubtful accounts was $882,000 and $710,000 as of December 31, 2015 and 2014, respectively. &nbsp;In regards to identifying uncollectible accounts, the Company reviews an aging report on a consistent basis to determine past due accounts, and utilizes a well established credit rating agency. &nbsp;The Company charges off those accounts that are deemed uncollectible once all collection efforts have been exhausted.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Inventories
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Inventories are valued at the lower of cost or market. &nbsp;The cost of inventories is determined by the first-in, first-out (FIFO) method. The Company generally considers inventory quantities beyond two years of non-usage, measured on a historical usage basis, to be excess inventory and reduces the carrying value of inventory accordingly.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Property and Equipment
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Property and equipment are carried at cost. Depreciation and amortization are computed using the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the assets or, for leasehold improvements, the life of the lease, if shorter. When assets are retired or otherwise disposed of, the cost and related accumulated depreciation are removed from the accounts and any resulting gain or loss is reflected in other income or expense for the period. The cost of maintenance and repairs is expensed as incurred; significant improvements are capitalized.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Goodwill
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
	In accordance with Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) ASC Topic 350, Intangibles
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8211;
</FONT>
	Goodwill and Other, the Company performed an annual impairment test in accordance with this guidance as of December 31, 2015 and also at December 31, 2014. &nbsp;These analyses did not indicate any impairment of goodwill at the end of either period.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Stock-Based Compensation Plans
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6.667PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In 2006, the Company adopted a Phantom Stock Plan (the
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	Plan
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	), which allows the Company to grant phantom stock units (Units) to certain key employees, officers or directors. &nbsp;The Units each represent a contractual right to payment of compensation in the future based upon the market value of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s common stock. &nbsp;The Units follow a vesting schedule of three years from the grant date, and are then paid upon maturity. &nbsp;In accordance with FASB ASC Topic 718, Stock Compensation, the Company uses the Black-Scholes option pricing model as its method for determining the fair value of the Units. &nbsp;Further details of the Plan are provided in Note 12.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=CENTER>
	-31-
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">

<HR STYLE="MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX; PADDING-TOP:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage32"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<B>
<U>
	Product Liability Reserves
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Product liability reserves represent the estimated unpaid amounts under the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s insurance policies with respect to existing claims. The Company uses the most current available data to estimate claims. As explained more fully under Note 11, Commitments and Contingencies, for various product liability claims covered under the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s general liability insurance policies, the Company must pay certain defense and settlement costs within its deductible or self-insured retention limits, ranging primarily from $25,000 to $250,000 per claim, depending on the terms of the policy in the applicable policy year, up to an aggregate amount. The Company is vigorously defending against all known claims.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Fair Value of Financial and Nonfinancial Instruments
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company measures financial instruments in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 820, Fair Value Measurements and Disclosures. The accounting standard defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair value under GAAP, and enhances disclosures about fair value measurements. Fair value is defined as the exchange price that would be received for an asset or paid to transfer a liability (an exit price) in the principal or most advantageous market for the asset or liability in an orderly transaction between market participants on the measurement date. Valuation techniques used to measure fair value must maximize the use of observable inputs and minimize the use of unobservable inputs. &nbsp;The standard creates a fair value hierarchy which prioritizes the inputs to valuation techniques used to measure fair value into three broad levels as follows: Level 1 inputs are quoted prices (unadjusted) in active markets for identical assets or liabilities; Level 2 inputs are inputs other than quoted prices included within Level 1 that are observable for the asset or liability, either directly or indirectly; and Level 3 inputs are unobservable inputs that reflect the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s own assumptions about the assumptions market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability. The Company relies on its actively traded share value
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8211;
</FONT>
	a level 1 input
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8211;
</FONT>
	in determining the fair value of the reporting unit in its annual impairment test as described in the FASB ASC Topic 350, Intangibles - Goodwill and Other.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Advertising Expense
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Advertising costs are charged to operations as incurred and are included in selling expenses in the accompanying consolidated Statement of Operations. &nbsp;Such charges aggregated $1,062,000 and $848,000, for the years ended December 31, 2015, and 2014, respectively. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Research and Development Expense
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Research and development expenses are charged to operations as incurred. Such charges totaled $876,000, and $904,000, for the years ended December 31, 2015 and 2014, respectively and are included in engineering expense in the accompanying consolidated statements of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Shipping Costs
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Shipping costs are included in selling expense on the consolidated statements of operations. The expense relating to shipping was $2,429,000 and $2,280,000 for the years ended December 31, 2015 and 2014, respectively.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Earnings per Common Share
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Basic earnings per share have been computed using the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding. For the periods presented, there are no dilutive securities. &nbsp;Consequently, basic and dilutive earnings per share are the same.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">

<A NAME="eolPage33"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<B>
<U>
	Currency Translation
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Assets and liabilities denominated in foreign currencies, most of which relate to our United Kingdom subsidiary whose functional currency is British pound sterling, are translated into U.S. dollars at exchange rates prevailing on the balance sheet dates. The statements of operations are translated into U.S. dollars at average exchange rates for the period. Adjustments resulting from the translation of financial statements are excluded from the determination of income and are accumulated in a separate component of shareholders
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	equity. &nbsp;For the years ended December 31, 2015 and 2014, exchange gains and losses resulting from foreign currency transactions were not significant and are included in the statements of operations (other income (expense)) in the period in which they occur.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Income Taxes
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company accounts for tax liabilities in accordance with the FASB ASC Topic 740, Income Taxes. Under this method the Company recorded tax expense, related deferred taxes and tax benefits, and uncertainties in tax positions.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax consequences attributable to differences between the financial statement carrying amounts of existing assets and liabilities and their respective tax bases. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the years in which those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. The effect on deferred tax assets and liabilities from a change in tax rates is recognized in income in the period that includes the enactment date. A valuation allowance is provided for deferred tax assets if it is more likely than not that these items will either expire before the Company is able to realize the benefit, or that future deductibility is uncertain.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The FASB ASC Topic 740, Income Taxes, clarifies the criteria that an individual tax position must satisfy for some or all of the benefits of that position to be recognized in a company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s financial statements. This guidance prescribes a recognition threshold of more-likely than-not, and a measurement attribute for all tax positions taken or expected to be taken on a tax return, in order for those tax positions to be recognized in the financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company follows the provisions of ASC 740-10 relative to accounting for uncertainties in tax positions. These provisions provide guidance on the recognition, de-recognition and measurement of potential tax benefits associated with tax positions. The Company elected to recognize interest and penalties related to income tax matters as a component of the income tax provision in the consolidated statements of income. For additional information regarding ASC 740-10, see Note 8.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The FASB ASU 2015-17 eliminates the current requirement for organizations to present deferred tax liabilities and assets as current and noncurrent in a classified balance sheet. &nbsp;Instead, organizations will be required to classify all deferred tax assets and liabilities as noncurrent. &nbsp;The amendments of ASU 2015-17 apply to all organizations that present a classified balance sheet. &nbsp;For public companies, the amendments are effective for financial statements issued for annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016, and interim periods within those annual periods. &nbsp;Early adoption is permitted and the Company adopted this ASU prospectively in calendar year ended December 31, 2015. &nbsp;As a result, the Company has presented all deferred tax assets and liabilities as noncurrent on its consolidated balance sheet as of December 31, 2015, but the Company has not reclassified deferred tax assets and liabilities on its consolidated balance sheet as of December 31, 2014. &nbsp;There was no impact on operations as a result of adoption of FASB ASU 2015-17.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Other Comprehensive Income
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	For the years ended December 31, 2015 and 2014, respectively, the components of other comprehensive income consisted solely of foreign currency translation adjustments.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Significant Concentration
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	One customer accounted for approximately 16% of sales in 2015 and 15% in 2014. &nbsp;That same customer accounted for 25% and 21% of Accounts Receivable at December 31, 2015 and 2014, respectively. &nbsp;No other customer represented more that 10% of Accounts Receivable or Sales. &nbsp;Also, during 2015 and 2014, approximately 88% of sales occurred in North America, with the remaining 12% portion scattered among other countries, but mostly pertaining to the United Kingdom.
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<B>
<U>
	Subsequent Events
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company evaluates all events or transactions through the date of the related filing that may have a material impact on its consolidated financial statements. &nbsp;Refer to Note 13 of the consolidated financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
<U>
	Recent Accounting Pronouncements
</U>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In May 2014, the FASB issued ASU 2014-09,
<I>
	Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606)
</I>
	, requiring an entity to recognize the amount of revenue to which it expects to be entitled for the transfer of promised goods or services to customers. The updated standard will replace most existing revenue recognition guidance in U.S. GAAP when it becomes effective and permits the use of either a full retrospective or retrospective with cumulative effect transition method. The updated standard becomes effective for the Company in the first quarter of fiscal year 2018. Early adoption is permitted beginning in the first quarter of the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s 2017 fiscal year. &nbsp;The Company has not yet selected a transition method and is currently evaluating the effect that the updated standard will have on the consolidated financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In July 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-11,
<I>
	Simplifying the Measurement of Inventory (Topic 330)
</I>
	. &nbsp;Under this ASU, inventory will be measured at the
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	lower of cost and net realizable value
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	and options that currently exist for
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	market value
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	will be eliminated. The ASU defines net realizable value as the
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	estimated selling prices in the ordinary course of business, less reasonably predictable costs of completion, disposal, and transportation.
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	No other changes were made to the current guidance on inventory measurement. ASU 2015-11 is effective for interim and annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016. Early application is permitted and should be applied prospectively. &nbsp;The Company is evaluating the provisions of this statement, including which period to adopt, and has not determined what impact the adoption of ASU 2015-11 will have on the Company's financial position or results of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-02,
<I>
	Leases (Topic 842)
</I>
	. &nbsp;Under this ASU, lessees are required to recognize right-of-use assets and lease liabilities for all leases not considered short-term leases. By definition, a short-term lease is one in which: (a) the lease term is 12 months or less and (b) there is not an option to purchase the underlying asset that the lessee is reasonably certain to exercise. For short-term leases, lessees may elect an accounting policy by class of underlying asset under which right-of-use assets and lease liabilities are not recognized and lease payments are generally recognized as expense over the lease term on a straight-line basis. This change will result in lessees recognizing right-of-use assets and lease liabilities for most leases currently accounted for as operating leases under the legacy lease accounting guidance. &nbsp;ASU 2016-02 is effective for interim and annual periods beginning after December 15, 2018. &nbsp;Early adoption is permitted. The Company is evaluating the provisions of this statement, including which period to adopt, and has not determined what impact the adoption of ASU 2016-02 will have on the Company's financial position or results of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT; COLOR:#1F497D">
	&#160;
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
	5. LINE OF CREDIT
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 29, 2014, the Company entered into to an Amended and Restated Committed Revolving Line of Credit Note (
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	the Line
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	) and a Second Amendment to the Loan Agreement with Santander Bank, N.A. (
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8220;
</FONT>
	Santander
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8221;
</FONT>
	). The Company renewed and increased the Line facility in the maximum amount of $15,000,000, for a five year term maturing on December 31, 2019, with funds available for working capital purposes and to fund dividends. This Line facility supersedes the expiring $10,000,000 line of credit the Company previously had in place with Santander since 2010. The Line is unsecured. The Line provides for the payment of any borrowings at an interest rate of either LIBOR plus 1.00% to plus 1.35% (for borrowings with a fixed term of 30, 60, or 90 days), or Prime from 0.00% to plus 0.10%, depending upon the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s then existing financial ratios. &nbsp;At December 31, 2015, the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s financial ratios would allow for the most favorable rate under the agreement
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s range, which would be a rate of 1.61%. Under the terms of the agreement, the Company is required to pay on a quarterly basis an unused facility fee equal to 10 basis points of the average unused balance of the total Line commitment.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	As of December 31, 2015 and December 31, 2014, the Company had no outstanding borrowings on its line of credit, and was in compliance with all debt covenants.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>

	As of December 31, 2015 and December 31, 2014, the Company had authorized 20,000,000 common stock shares with par value of $0.01 per share. &nbsp;At both dates, the number of shares issued was 10,153,633, and the total number of outstanding shares was 10,091,822, with the 61,811 variance representing shares held in Treasury.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 10, 2015, the Board declared a special dividend of $0.85 per share to all Shareholders of record as of December 21, 2015, and payable on or before January 6, 2016. The Company paid its transfer agent $8,578,000 on January 5, 2016, and the transfer agent paid the shareholders on January 6, 2016.
</P>

<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 10, 2014, the Board declared a special dividend of $0.49 per share to all Shareholders of record as of December 22, 2014, which was paid on January 5, 2015, in the amount of $4,945,000. &nbsp;Additionally, there was a dividend that was paid during 2014 by the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s UK subsidiary, which amounted to an outlay of cash of $145,000 to the subsidiary
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s noncontrolling interest.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 9, 2013, the Board declared a special dividend of $0.425 per share to all Shareholders of record as of December 19, 2013, and payable on or before January 2, 2014. The Company paid its transfer agent $4,289,000 on December 31, 2013, and the transfer agent paid the shareholders on January 2, 2014.

<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s Board of Directors authorized an extension of its stock repurchase program without expiration, up to a maximum amount of $1,000,000. &nbsp;The original program established in December of 2007 authorized the purchase of up to $5,000,000 of its common stock. &nbsp;The purchases may be made from time-to-time in the open market or in privately negotiated transactions, depending on market and business conditions. &nbsp;The Board retained the right to cancel, extend, or expand the share buyback program, at any time and from time-to-time. &nbsp;Since inception, the Company has purchased a total of 61,811 shares for approximately $932,000, or approximately $15 per share. &nbsp;The Company did not make any stock repurchases during the year ended December 31, 2015 or 2014.

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Pre-tax income included foreign income of $4,117,000 and $3,474,000 in 2015 and 2014, respectively. &nbsp;During 2014, the Company paid a dividend out of its U.K. subsidiary, resulting in incremental U.S. taxes of $296,000. &nbsp;As of December 31, 2015, the Company has $4,561,000 of unremitted earnings at its foreign subsidiaries. &nbsp;The Company has not provided deferred taxes on these amounts, as the Company considers these balances to be indefinitely invested in the operations of the foreign subsidiary. The incremental U.S. tax that would be paid if these earnings were remitted is $738,000. &nbsp;
</P>

	Management believes it is more likely than not that the Company will have sufficient taxable income when these timing differences reverse and that the deferred tax assets will be realized and, accordingly, no valuation allowance is deemed necessary.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company is currently subject to audit by the Internal Revenue Service for the calendar years ended 2012 through 2014. The Company and its Subsidiaries
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	state income tax returns are subject to audit for the calendar years ended 2011 through 2014.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	As of December 31, 2015, the Company had provided a liability of $110,000 for unrecognized tax benefits related to various federal and state income tax matters, which is included in Other Long Term Liabilities. Of this amount, the amount that would impact the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s effective tax rate, if recognized, was $71,000. The liability for unrecognized tax benefits at December 31, 2014 was $105,000. &nbsp;Of this amount, the amount that would impact the Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s effective tax rate, if recognized, was $68,000. The difference between the total amount of unrecognized tax benefits and the amount that would impact the effective tax rate consists of items that are offset by the federal tax benefits of state income tax items of $39,000 and $37,000 for 2015 and 2014, respectively.
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT">
<B>
	9. LEASES
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In the United States, the Company owns its main operating facility located at 451 Creamery Way in Exton, PA, but the Company does however also lease additional manufacturing, warehousing and distribution space in Exton, which is under contract through January of 2018. &nbsp;During 2014, the Company obtained a new five year lease on a warehousing and distribution center in Houston, Texas. &nbsp;Additionally, the Company leases its corporate office space in Middletown, CT.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In the United Kingdom, the Company leases a facility in Banbury, England, which serves sales, warehousing and operational functions. &nbsp;The lease in Banbury was effective April 1, 2006 and has a 15-year term ending in March 2021. There is an option to terminate the lease in December of 2017. &nbsp;Termination in 2017 requires a penalty of 2 months rentals, or approximately $40,000. &nbsp;The Company
<FONT STYLE="FONT-FAMILY:'ARIAL UNICODE MS,TIMES NEW ROMAN'">
	&#8217;
</FONT>
	s current intention is to utilize the facility for the 15 years.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In addition to property rentals, the Company also leases several automobiles, which are included in the rent expense and in the operating lease details below.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Rent expense for operating leases was approximately $504,000 and $475,000 for the years ended December 31, 2015, and 2014, respectively.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:16PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:12PT" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Future minimum lease payments under non-cancelable leases as of December 31, 2015 is as follows:
</P>
